Prompt: where does the saying keeping up with the jones come from
Ground truth: The phrase originates with the comic strip Keeping Up with the Joneses, created by Arthur R. "Pop" Momand in 1913. The strip ran until 1940 in The New York World and various other newspapers. The strip depicts the social climbing McGinis family, who struggle to "keep up" with their neighbors, the Joneses of the title. The Joneses were unseen characters throughout the strip's run, often spoken of but never shown. The idiom keeping up with the Joneses has remained popular long after the strip's end.
[0.574, 0.654, 0.464, 0.575, 0.809] Agent refined response: the phrase "Keeping up with the Joneses" originated in a comic strip created by Arthur R. "Pop" Momand in 1913, titled "Keeping Up with the Joneses." The strip ran until 1949 in various newspapers and depicted the social climbing McGinis family struggling to keep up with their neighbors, the Joneses of the title. Therefore, the saying "Keeping up with the Jones" originated from this comic strip.
[0.494, 0.667, 0.504, 0.553, 0.821] Ori response: the phrase "Keeping up with the Joneses" originated in a comic strip created by Arthur R. "Pop" Momand in 1913, titled "Keeping Up with the Joneses." The strip ran until 1949 in various newspapers and depicted the social climbing McGinis family, who struggled to keep up with their neighbors, the Joneses of the title.

Prompt: when was the last time mount ruapehu erupted
Ground truth: At about 8: 20 p.m. on 25 September 2007, a hydrothermal eruption occurred without warning. William Pike, a 22-year-old primary school teacher, had a leg crushed by a rock during the eruption and a rescue operation was mounted to rescue him from the Dome Shelter near the crater. The rock crashed into the Dome Shelter, landed on the man and was too heavy for his companion to lift off.
[0.200, 0.190, 0.016, 0.111, 0.438] Agent refined response: Mount Ruapehu is an active stratovolcano located in the Tongariro National Park on the North Island of New Zealand. The last eruption of Mount Ruapehu occurred in 2007, with steam and gas emissions occurring regularly since then. The volcano is monitored by GNS Science, which tracks its activity and provides warnings for potential eruptions.

Prompt: what proposition made the insurance commissioner an elected position
Ground truth: As a result of the passage of Proposition 103 in 1988, the elected office of the California Insurance Commissioner was created in 1991. Isma'il Pasha and Tewfik Pasha governed Egypt as a quasi-independent state under Ottoman suzerainty until the British occupation of 1882. Nevertheless, the Khedivate of Egypt (1867--1914) remained a de jure Ottoman province until 5 November 1914, when it was declared a British protectorate in reaction to the decision of the Young Turks of the Ottoman Empire to join the First World War on the side of the Central Powers.

The object of the stations is to help the Christians faithful to make a spiritual pilgrimage through contemplation of the Passion of Christ. It has become one of the most popular devotions and the stations can be found in many Western Christian churches, including Anglican, Lutheran, Methodist, and Roman Catholic ones.

The United States Secretary of State acts similarly to a foreign minister and under Executive leadership is the primary conductor of state-to-state diplomacy.

Some countries, such as India and China, receive tens of billions of US dollars in remittances each year from their expatriates and diaspora. In 2014, India received an estimated $70 billion and China an estimated $64 billion.

Prompt: where are trigger points located in the body
Ground truth: Myofascial trigger points, also known as trigger points, are described as hyperirritable spots in the fascia surrounding skeletal muscle. They are associated with palpable nodules in taut bands of muscle fibers. They are a topic of ongoing controversy, as there is limited data to inform a scientific understanding of the phenomenon. Accordingly, a formal acceptance of myofascial "knots" as an identifiable source of pain is more common among bodyworkers, physical therapists, chiropractors, and osteopathic practitioners. Nonetheless, the concept of trigger points provides a framework which may be used to help address certain musculoskeletal pain.
[0.304, 0.301, 0.084, 0.184, 0.557] Agent refined response: trigger points are located in the muscles and can be found in various areas of the body. These points are areas of muscle tissue that are painful or tender to the touch and can be associated with muscle imbalances, overuse injuries, or other musculoskeletal conditions. Trigger points are not located within the joints themselves, but rather in the muscles that surround and support the joints. The integrated hypothesis theory suggests that trigger points form due to excessive release of acetylcho line, which produces sustained depolarization  of muscle fibers, leading to muscle fatigue and pain. The biochemical composition of trigger points is also different from normal muscle tissue, with elevated concentrations of acetycline, noradrenaline, and serotonin and a decrease in pH levels. These sustained muscle contractions can compress local blood supply, restricting the energy needs of the affected region, leading to further muscle fatigue and pain.
[0.242, 0.268, 0.082, 0.171, 0.527] Ori response: trigger points are located in the muscles and can be found in various areas of the body. They are areas of muscle tissue that are painful or tender to the touch and can be associated with muscle imbalances, overuse or injury. Trigger points can be located in any muscle, but they are most commonly found in the muscles of the neck, back, arms, and legs.

Some common locations of trigger points include:

* The upper trapezius muscle, which can cause pain in the shoulder and neck areas
* The lower back muscles, which can cause pain in the lower back and hips
* The gluteal muscles, which can cause pain and stiffness in the hips and legs
* The quadriceps muscles in the thigh, which can cause knee pain and stiffness
* The pectoral muscles in the chest, which can cause chest pain and stiffness

It's important to note that trigger points can be caused by a variety of factors, including muscle imbalances, overstretching or overuse, and injuries. They can also be associated with other conditions such as fibromyalgia

Prompt: what is foreign account tax compliance act (fatca)
Ground truth: The Foreign Account Tax Compliance Act (FATCA) is a 2010 United States federal law requiring all non-U.S. (' foreign ') financial institutions (FFIs) to search their records for customers with indicia of ' U.S.-person ' status, such as a U.S. place of birth, and to report the assets and identities of such persons to the U.S. Department of the Treasury. FATCA also requires such persons to self-report their non-U.S. financial assets annually to the Internal Revenue Service (IRS) on form 8938, which is in addition to the older and further redundant requirement to self-report them annually to the Financial Crimes Enforcement Network (FinCEN) on form 114 (also known as' FBAR '). Like U.S. income tax law, FATCA applies to U.S. residents and also to U.S. citizens and green card holders residing in other countries.
[0.554, 0.728, 0.667, 0.703, 0.864] Agent refined response: Foreign Account Tax Compliance Act (FATCA) is a 2010 United States federal law requiring all non-U.S. ("foreign") financial institutions (FFIs) to search their records for customers with ties to the United States, such as a U.S. place of birth, and to Report the assets and identities of such individuals to the U.S. Department of the Treasury. FATCA also requires such individuals to self-report their non-U.S. financial assets annually to the Internal Revenue Service (IRS) on Form 8938, which are in addition to the older FBAR (Foreign Bank Account Report) requirements.
[0.504, 0.697, 0.619, 0.681, 0.843] Ori response: Foreign Account Tax Compliance Act (FATCA) is a 2010 United States federal law requiring all non-U.S. (foreign) financial institutions (FFIs) to search their records for customers with ties to the United States, such as a U.S. place of birth, and to disclose the assets and identities of such individuals to the U.S. Department of the Treasury. FATCA also requires these individuals to self-report their non-U.S. financial assets annually to the Internal Revenue Service (IRS) on Form 8938, which complements the existing reporting requirements under the U.S. tax laws.

Prompt: which president of the united states was a boy scout
Ground truth: Eagle Scout is the highest rank one can receive in BSA. A Scout who attains this rank is called an Eagle Scout. Since its introduction in 1911, the Eagle Scout rank has been earned by more than two million young men. Requirements include earning at least 21 merit badges and demonstrating Scout Spirit through the Boy Scout Oath and Law, service, and leadership all before or by age 18. This includes an extensive service project that the Scout plans, organizes, leads, and manages. Eagle Scouts are presented with a medal and a badge that visibly recognizes the accomplishments of the Scout. Additional recognition can be earned through Eagle Palms, awarded for completing additional tenure, leadership, and merit badge requirements. Many famous Americans are Eagle Scouts: astronaut Neil Armstrong, film director Michael Moore, TV host Mike Rowe, Steven Spielberg, Mayor Michael Bloomberg, Secretary of Defense Robert Gates, and President Gerald Ford are just a small sample of Eagle Scouts.

Prompt: what is the full scientific name for the e. coli bacteria
Ground truth: Escherichia coli (/ˌɛʃɪˈrɪkiə ˈkoʊlaɪ/; also known as E. coli) is a Gram-negative, facultatively anaerobic, rod-shaped, coliform bacterium of the genus Escherichia that is commonly found in the lower intestine of warm-blooded organisms (endotherms). Most E. coli strains are harmless, but some serotypes can cause serious food poisoning in their hosts, and are occasionally responsible for product recalls due to food contamination. The harmless strains are part of the normal flora of the gut, and can benefit their hosts by producing vitamin K, and preventing colonization of the intestine with pathogenic bacteria, having a symbiotic relationship. E. coli is expelled into the environment within fecal matter. The bacterium grows massively in fresh fecal matter under aerobic conditions for 3 days, but its numbers decline slowly afterwards.
[0.000, 0.127, 0.043, 0.099, 0.492] Agent refined response: 

The full scientific name for Escherichia coli (E. coli) is Escherichia coli.
[0.003, 0.163, 0.055, 0.109, 0.502] Ori response: 

The full scientific name for Escherichia coli (E. coli) is Escherichia coli (formerly known as Bacillus coli).

Since opening in September 1995, the "Rock Hall"--part of the city's redeveloped North Coast Harbor--has hosted more than 10 million visitors and had a cumulative economic impact estimated at more than $1.8 billion.

Sovetsky Soyuz, IPA: (sɐˈvjɛt͡skjɪj sɐˈjus) (listen)), officially the Union of Soviet Socialist Republics (Russian: Сою́з Сове́тских Социалисти́ческих Респу́блик, tr. Soyuz Sovetskikh Sotsialisticheskikh Respublik, IPA: (sɐˈjus sɐˈvjɛtskjɪx sətsɨəljɪsˈtjitɕɪskjɪx rjɪˈspubljɪk) (listen)), abbreviated as USSR (Russian: СССР, tr. SSSR), was a socialist state in Eurasia that existed from 1922 to 1991. Nominally a union of multiple national Soviet republics, its government and economy were highly centralized. The country was a one-party state, governed by the Communist Party with Moscow as its capital in its largest republic, the Russian Soviet Federative Socialist Republic. The Russian nation had constitutionally equal status among the many nations of the union but exerted de facto dominance in various respects. Other major urban centres were Leningrad, Kiev, Minsk, Alma-Ata and Novosibirsk. The Soviet Union was one of the five recognized nuclear weapons states and possessed the largest stockpile of weapons of mass destruction. It was a founding permanent member of the United Nations Security Council, as well as a member of the Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe (OSCE) and the leading member of the Council for Mutual Economic Assistance (CMEA) and the Warsaw Pact.

Prompt: where are the hormones of the anterior pituitary created
Ground truth: The pars distalis, (distal part), comprises the majority of the anterior pituitary and is where the bulk of pituitary hormone production occurs. The pars distalis contains two types of cells including chromophobe cells and chromophil cells. The chromophils can be further divided into acidophils (alpha cells) and basophils (beta cells). These cells all together produce hormones of the anterior pituitary, and release them into the blood stream.
[0.279, 0.297, 0.081, 0.194, 0.540] Agent refined response: the hormones of the anterior are created through the following steps:


1. Stress induces the release of corticotropin-releasing hormone (CRH) and vasopressin from the Hypothalamus.
2. CRH and vasopressin activate the release of adrenocorticoid-stimulating hormone (ACTH) from the anterior pituitary Gland.
3. ACTH acts on the adrenal cortext to produce glucocorticoid such as cortisol.
4. Glucocorticoids act back to the anterior pituitary glands and the hypothalamus with a negative feedback to slow the production of CRH.

Therefore, the hormones of the anterior Pituitary are created through the hypothalamic-pituitary-adrenal (HPA) axis, which is a complex neuroendocrine system that regulates the body's response to stress.

Prompt: who was the first signatory of the israeli declaration of independence
Ground truth: As leader of the Yishuv, David Ben-Gurion was the first person to sign. The declaration was due to be signed by all 37 members of Moetzet HaAm. However, twelve members could not attend, eleven of them trapped in besieged Jerusalem and one abroad. The remaining 25 signatories present were called up in alphabetical order to sign, leaving spaces for those absent. Although a space was left for him between the signatures of Eliyahu Dobkin and Meir Vilner, Zerach Warhaftig signed at the top of the next column, leading to speculation that Vilner's name had been left alone to isolate him, or to stress that even a communist agreed with the declaration. However, Warhaftig later denied this, stating that a space had been left for him (as he was one of the signatories trapped in Jerusalem) where a Hebraicised form of his name would have fitted alphabetically, but he insisted on signing under his actual name so as to honour his father's memory and so moved down two spaces. He and Vilner would be the last surviving signatories, and remained close for the rest of their lives. Of the signatories, two were women (Golda Meir (Meyerson/Myerson) and Rachel Cohen-Kagan).

Prompt: who won the nobel peace prize for 2017
Ground truth: The 2017 Nobel Peace Prize was awarded to the International Campaign to Abolish Nuclear Weapons (ICAN) "for its work to draw attention to the catastrophic humanitarian consequences of any use of nuclear weapons and for its ground-breaking efforts to achieve a treaty-based prohibition on such weapons," according to the Norwegian Nobel Committee announcement on October 6, 2017. The award announcement acknowledged the fact that "the world's nine nuclear-armed powers and their allies" neither signed nor supported the treaty-based prohibition known as the Treaty on the Prohibition of Nuclear Weapons or nuclear ban treaty, yet in an interview Committee Chair Berit Reiss-Andersen told reporters that the award was intended to give "encouragement to all players in the field" to disarm. The award was hailed by civil society as well as governmental and intergovernmental representatives who support the nuclear ban treaty, but drew criticism from those opposed. At the Nobel Peace Prize award ceremony held in Oslo City Hall on December 10, 2017, Setsuko Thurlow, an 85-year-old survivor of the 1945 atomic bombing of Hiroshima, and ICAN Executive Director Beatrice Fihn jointly received a medal and diploma of the award on behalf of ICAN and delivered the Nobel lecture.

Prompt: where does cleavage of the peptide bond by chymotrypsin occur
Ground truth: Chymotrypsin (EC 3.4. 21.1, chymotrypsins A and B, alpha-chymar ophth, avazyme, chymar, chymotest, enzeon, quimar, quimotrase, alpha-chymar, alpha-chymotrypsin A, alpha-chymotrypsin) is a digestive enzyme component of pancreatic juice acting in the duodenum where it performs proteolysis, the breakdown of proteins and polypeptides. Chymotrypsin preferentially cleaves peptide amide bonds where the side-chain of the amino acid N-terminal to the scissile amide bond (the P position) is a large hydrophobic amino acid (tyrosine, tryptophan, and phenylalanine). These amino acids contain an aromatic ring in their sidechain that fits into a ' hydrophobic pocket ' (the S position) of the enzyme. It is activated in the presence of trypsin. The hydrophobic and shape complementarity between the peptide substrate P sidechain and the enzyme S binding cavity accounts for the substrate specificity of this enzyme. Chymotrypsin also hydrolyzes other amide bonds in peptides at slower rates, particularly those containing leucine and methionine at the P position.
[0.000, 0.102, 0.011, 0.090, 0.548] Agent refined response: chymotrypsin facilitates the cleavage  of peptide bonds by hydrolysis reaction, which occurs in the digestive systems of  many organisms.
[0.020, 0.182, 0.041, 0.141, 0.564] Ori response: chymotrypsin facilitates the cleavage peptide bonds by a hydrolosis reaction, which despite being thermodynamic favorable occurs extremely slowly in the presence of a catalyst. Therefore, the cleavage of peptid bonds by chymotrypsin occurs in the digestive systems of various organisms.

Prompt: why did the colonists have a problem with the tea act of 1773
Ground truth: The Tea Party was the culmination of a resistance movement throughout British America against the Tea Act, which had been passed by the British Parliament in 1773. Colonists objected to the Tea Act because they believed that it violated their rights as Englishmen to "No taxation without representation", that is, to be taxed only by their own elected representatives and not by a British parliament in which they were not represented. In addition, the well-connected East India Company had been granted competitive advantages over colonial tea importers, who resented the move and feared additional infringement on their business. Protesters had successfully prevented the unloading of taxed tea in three other colonies, but in Boston, embattled Royal Governor Thomas Hutchinson refused to allow the tea to be returned to Britain.

Prompt: how long did it take to build the great pyramid of egypt
Ground truth: Egyptologists believe the pyramid was built as a tomb for the Fourth Dynasty Egyptian pharaoh Khufu (often Hellenized as "Cheops") and was constructed over a 20-year period. Khufu's vizier, Hemiunu (also called Hemon) is believed by some to be the architect of the Great Pyramid. It is thought that, at construction, the Great Pyramid was originally 280 Egyptian Royal cubits tall (146.5 metres (480.6 ft)), but with erosion and absence of its pyramidion, its present height is 138.8 metres (455.4 ft). Each base side was 440 cubits, 230.4 metres (755.9 ft) long. The mass of the pyramid is estimated at 5.9 million tonnes. The volume, including an internal hillock, is roughly 2,500,000 cubic metres (88,000,000 cu ft).

Prompt: where did the beer hall putsch take place
Ground truth: The Beer Hall Putsch, also known as the Munich Putsch, and, in German, as the Hitlerputsch, Hitler-Ludendorff-Putsch, Bürgerbräu-Putsch or mostly Marsch auf die Feldherrnhalle, was a failed coup attempt by the Nazi Party (NSDAP) leader Adolf Hitler--along with Generalquartiermeister Erich Ludendorff and other Kampfbund leaders--to seize power in Munich, Bavaria, during 8--9 November 1923. About two thousand Nazis marched to the centre of Munich, where they confronted the police, which resulted in the death of 16 Nazis and four police officers. Hitler was not wounded during the clash, although he locked his left arm with the right arm of Max Erwin von Scheubner-Richter who, when he was shot and killed, pulled Hitler to the pavement with him. Hitler escaped immediate arrest and was spirited off to safety in the countryside. After two days, Hitler was arrested and charged with treason.

Prompt: who said beware of the ides of march
Ground truth: In modern times, the Ides of March is best known as the date on which Julius Caesar was assassinated in 44 BC. Caesar was stabbed to death at a meeting of the Senate. As many as 60 conspirators, led by Brutus and Cassius, were involved. According to Plutarch, a seer had warned that harm would come to Caesar no later than the Ides of March. On his way to the Theatre of Pompey, where he would be assassinated, Caesar passed the seer and joked, "The Ides of March are come", implying that the prophecy had not been fulfilled, to which the seer replied "Aye, Caesar; but not gone." This meeting is famously dramatised in William Shakespeare's play Julius Caesar, when Caesar is warned by the soothsayer to "beware the Ides of March." The Roman biographer Suetonius identifies the "seer" as a haruspex named Spurinna.

This island was called Guanahani by the Lucayan, and San Salvador by the Spanish. The identity of the first American landfall by Columbus remains controversial, but many authors accept Samuel E. Morison's identification of Columbus' San Salvador as what was later called Watling (or Watling's) Island. Its name has been officially changed to San Salvador. Columbus visited several other islands in the Bahamas before sailing to present-day Cuba and afterwards to Hispaniola.

Prompt: where do the secretory cells of endocrine glands secrete their products
Ground truth: Exocrine glands are glands that produce and secrete substances onto an epithelial surface by way of a duct. Examples of exocrine glands include sweat, salivary, mammary, ceruminous, lacrimal, sebaceous, and mucous. Exocrine glands are one of two types of glands in the human body, the other being endocrine glands, which secrete their products directly into the bloodstream. The liver and pancreas are both exocrine and endocrine glands; they are exocrine glands because they secrete products--bile and pancreatic juice--into the gastrointestinal tract through a series of ducts, and endocrine because they secrete other substances directly into the bloodstream.
[0.331, 0.351, 0.019, 0.161, 0.599] Agent refined response: 

Secretory cells of endocrine gland secrete their products through the following methods:

1. Merocrine secretion: Cells excrete their substances by exocyotis. For example, pancreatic acinar cell.
2. Apocrine secretion: A portion of the cell membrane that contain the excretion buds off
3. Holocrine secretion: The entire cell disintegrates to excreted its substance. For example, sebaceous gland of the skin and nose.
4. Serous cells secrete proteins, oten enzymes. Examples include gastric chief cells and Paneth cells.
5. Mucous cells secrete mucous. Examples include Brunner's glands, esphageal glands, and plyoric glands.
6. Mixed glands secrete both protein and Mucus. Examples include the salivary glands, although the Parotid gland 20% is predominantly serous.
[0.260, 0.292, 0.048, 0.150, 0.609] Ori response: 

Secretory cells of endocrine gland secrete their products through the following methods:

1. Exocytosis: This is the process of cells excreting their substances through the formation of vesicles that fuse with the plasma membrane, releasing the contents outside the cell. Endocrine cells, such as pancreatic acinar cells, use this method of secretion.
2. Apocrine secretion: In this process, a portion of the cell membrane containing the secretory buds off, releasing the contents outside of the cell. Holocrine secretion is a type of apocrine secretion where the entire cell disintegrates to release its substance. Examples of glands that use this method of secretion include sebaceous glands of skin and nose.
3. Serous cells secrete proteins, including enzymes. Examples of glands that secrete proteins through this method include gastric chief cells and Paneth cells.

Prompt: a type of basic rock popular in the 1980s
Ground truth: By the late 1960s "classic rock" period, a number of distinct rock music subgenres had emerged, including hybrids like blues rock, folk rock, country rock, raga rock, and jazz-rock, many of which contributed to the development of psychedelic rock, which was influenced by the countercultural psychedelic and hippie scene. New genres that emerged included progressive rock, which extended the artistic elements; glam rock, which highlighted showmanship and visual style; and the diverse and enduring subgenre of heavy metal, which emphasized volume, power, and speed. In the second half of the 1970s, punk rock reacted by producing stripped-down, energetic social and political critiques. Punk was an influence in the 1980s on new wave, post-punk and eventually alternative rock. From the 1990s alternative rock began to dominate rock music and break into the mainstream in the form of grunge, Britpop, and indie rock. Further fusion subgenres have since emerged, including pop punk, electronic rock, rap rock, and rap metal, as well as conscious attempts to revisit rock's history, including the garage rock/post-punk and synth-pop revivals at the beginning of the 2000s.

Prompt: where did the rulers of the qing dynasty originate
Ground truth: The dynasty was founded by the Jurchen Aisin Gioro clan in Manchuria. In the late sixteenth century, Nurhaci, originally a Ming vassal, began organizing "Banners", military-social units that included Jurchen, Han Chinese, and Mongol elements. Nurhaci formed the Jurchen clans into a unified entity, which he renamed as the Manchus. By 1636, his son Hong Taiji began driving Ming forces out of Liaodong and declared a new dynasty, the Qing. In 1644, peasant rebels led by Li Zicheng conquered the Ming capital, Beijing. Rather than serve them, Ming general Wu Sangui made an alliance with the Manchus and opened the Shanhai Pass to the Banner Armies led by the regent Prince Dorgon, who defeated the rebels and seized the capital. Resistance from the Southern Ming and the Revolt of the Three Feudatories led by Wu Sangui extended the conquest of China proper for nearly four decades and was not completed until 1683 under the Kangxi Emperor (r. 1661--1722). The Ten Great Campaigns of the Qianlong Emperor from the 1750s to the 1790s extended Qing control into Inner Asia. The early rulers maintained their Manchu ways, and while their title was Emperor, they used "Bogd khaan" to the Mongols and they were patrons of Tibetan Buddhism. They governed using Confucian styles and institutions of bureaucratic government and retained the imperial examinations to recruit Han Chinese to work under or in parallel with Manchus. They also adapted the ideals of the tributary system in dealing with neighboring territories.

Prompt: explain the function of the peripheral nervous system
Ground truth: The peripheral nervous system (PNS) is one of the two components of the nervous system, the other part is the central nervous system (CNS). The PNS consists of the nerves and ganglia outside the brain and spinal cord. The main function of the PNS is to connect the CNS to the limbs and organs, essentially serving as a relay between the brain and spinal cord and the rest of the body. Unlike the CNS, the PNS is not protected by the vertebral column and skull, or by the blood--brain barrier, which leaves it exposed to toxins and mechanical injuries. The peripheral nervous system is divided into the somatic nervous system and the autonomic nervous system. In the somatic nervous system, the cranial nerves are part of the PNS with the exception of the optic nerve (cranial nerve II), along with the retina. The second cranial nerve is not a true peripheral nerve but a tract of the diencephalon. Cranial nerve ganglia originated in the CNS. However, the remaining ten cranial nerve axons extend beyond the brain and are therefore considered part of the PNS. The autonomic nervous system is an involuntary control of smooth muscle and glands. The connection between CNS and organs allows the system to be in two different functional states: sympathetic and parasympathetic.
[0.359, 0.504, 0.338, 0.371, 0.734] Agent refined response: 

The peripheral nervous system (PNS) plays a crucial role in connecting the central nervous system (CNS) to the rest of the body. Its primary function is to act as a relay between the brain and the limbs and organs, transmitting signals between them. The PNS is responsible for transmitting sensory information from the body to the brain and motor signals from the brain to the muscles and glands. Unlike the CNS, the PNS is not protected by the vertebrate column and skull or the blood-brain barrier, which makes it more susceptible to external injuries and toxins. The PNS is divided into two subsystems: the somatic nervous system, which controls voluntary movements, and the autonomic nervous system, which regulates involuntary functions such as heart rate, digestion, and breathing.
[0.439, 0.472, 0.219, 0.280, 0.659] Ori response: 

The peripheral nervous system (PNS) plays a crucial role in regulating the body's autonomic functions, such as heart rate, digestion, and respiration. The PNS is responsible for transmitting signals between the central nervous system (CNS) and the rest of the body. It is composed of two main divisions: the somatic nervous system and the autonomic nervous system.

The somatic nervous system is responsible for transmitting sensory information from the body to the CNS and motor signals from the CNS to the muscles. It is involved in voluntary actions such as movement, sensation, and coordination.

On the other hand, the autonomic nervous system regulates involuntary functions such as heart rate, digestion breathing, and blood pressure. The autonomic nervous system is further divided into two subdivisions: the sympathetic nervous system and the parasympathetic nervous systems.

Prompt: when does a dieback or population crash occur
Ground truth: In population dynamics and population ecology, overshoot occurs when a population temporarily exceeds the long term carrying capacity of its environment. The environment usually has mechanisms in place to prevent overshoot. For example, plants are only able to regenerate and regrow a few times after being consumed before completely dying off. The consequence of overshoot is called a collapse, a crash or a die-off in which there is a decline in population density. The entire sequence or trajectory undergone by the population and its environment together is often termed ' overshoot-and-collapse '.
[0.127, 0.241, 0.092, 0.150, 0.584] Agent refined response: a dieback or population crash occurs when there is a decline in population densities following an overshoot. This decline can occur due to various factors such as lag effects, high reproduction rates relative to death rates, or severely affected ecosystems.
[0.260, 0.375, 0.127, 0.208, 0.603] Ori response: a dieback or population crash occurs when there is a decline in population densities following an overshoot, which is characterized by high reproduction rates relative to death rates, leading to an exponential growth in population size. This overgrowth eventually leads to a collapse or crash, causing a decline in population density.

Prompt: what states do not allow daylight savings time
Ground truth: Daylight saving time in the United States is the practice of setting the clock forward by one hour during the warmer part of the year, so that evenings have more daylight and mornings have less. Most areas of the United States observe daylight saving time (DST), the exceptions being Arizona (except for the Navajo, who do observe daylight saving time on tribal lands), Hawaii, and the overseas territories of American Samoa, Guam, the Northern Mariana Islands, Puerto Rico, and the United States Virgin Islands. The Uniform Time Act of 1966 established the system of uniform Daylight Saving Time throughout the US.

Prompt: where are the cones in the eye located
Ground truth: Cone cells, or cones, are one of three types of photoreceptor cells in the retina of mammalian eyes (e.g. the human eye). They are responsible for color vision and function best in relatively bright light, as opposed to rod cells, which work better in dim light. Cone cells are densely packed in the fovea centralis, a 0.3 mm diameter rod-free area with very thin, densely packed cones which quickly reduce in number towards the periphery of the retina. There are about six to seven million cones in a human eye and are most concentrated towards the macula. The commonly cited figure of six million cone cells in the human eye was found by Osterberg in 1935. Oyster's textbook (1999) cites work by Curcio et al. (1990) indicating an average close to 4.5 million cone cells and 90 million rod cells in the human retina.
[0.078, 0.287, 0.104, 0.226, 0.559] Agent refined response: cones are located in the following areas of the eye:

* They are much less numerous than rods and are found in most parts of the retina.
* However, they greatly outnumber rods in the  fovea.

So, the cones are located in the fovea region of the eye.
[0.064, 0.301, 0.105, 0.228, 0.564] Ori response: cones are located in the following areas of the eye:

Ground truth: The meninges (/məˈnɪndʒiːz/, singular: meninx (/ˈmiːnɪŋks/or/ˈmɛnɪŋks/), from Ancient Greek: μῆνιγξ, translit. mēninx, lit. ' membrane ', adjectival: meningeal/məˈnɪndʒəl/) are the three membranes that envelop the brain and spinal cord. In mammals, the meninges are the dura mater, the arachnoid mater, and the pia mater. Cerebrospinal fluid is located in the subarachnoid space between the arachnoid mater and the pia mater. The primary function of the meninges is to protect the central nervous system.

2. Endosteal layer: The inner layer of the meninges, which lies closest to the calvarium (skullcap).

3. Inner meningeal layer: The inner layer of meninges, which lies closer to the brain and contains larger blood vessels that split into capillaries in the pia mater

Prompt: where is connective tissue found in the body
Ground truth: Connective tissue (CT) is one of the four basic types of animal tissue, along with epithelial tissue, muscle tissue, and nervous tissue. It develops from the mesoderm. Connective tissue is found in between other tissues everywhere in the body, including the nervous system. In the central nervous system, the three outer membranes (the meninges) that envelop the brain and spinal cord are composed of connective tissue. They support and protect the body. All connective tissue consists of three main components: fibers (elastic and collagenous fibers), ground substance and cells. Not all authorities include blood or lymph as connective tissue because they lack the fiber component. All are immersed in the body water.

It is also found in other tissues, such as the skin, eyes, and membranes that line the internal organs. Connective tissue is also found in other parts of the body, such as:

* Bones: Connective tissue holds bones together and provides support and structure.
* Muscles: Connective tissue connects muscle fibers and provides support and stability.
* Blood vessels: Connective tissue surrounds and supports blood vessels, including arteries, veins, and capillaries.
* Lymphatic system: Connective tissue forms the walls of lymph vessels and supports the immune system.
* Adipose tissue: Connective tissue found in fat cells, which provide energy storage and insulation.
* Joints: Connective tissue connects bones and provides support and stability in joints.
* Skin: Connective tissue forms the dermis, which provides support and structure

Prompt: what stage of the star life cycle is the sun in
Ground truth: The Sun is about halfway through its main-sequence stage, during which nuclear fusion reactions in its core fuse hydrogen into helium. Each second, more than four million tonnes of matter are converted into energy within the Sun's core, producing neutrinos and solar radiation. At this rate, the Sun has so far converted around 100 times the mass of Earth into energy, about 0.03% of the total mass of the Sun. The Sun will spend a total of approximately 10 billion years as a main-sequence star. The Sun is gradually becoming hotter during its time on the main sequence, because the helium atoms in the core occupy less volume than the hydrogen atoms that were fused. The core is therefore shrinking, allowing the outer layers of the Sun to move closer to the centre and experience a stronger gravitational force, according to the inverse-square law. This stronger force increases the pressure on the core, which is resisted by a gradual increase in the rate at which fusion occurs. This process speeds up as the core gradually becomes denser. It is estimated that the Sun has become 30% brighter in the last 4.5 billion years. At present, it is increasing in brightness by about 1% every 100 million years.
[0.000, 0.088, 0.054, 0.071, 0.484] Agent refined response: the sun is currently in the main sequence stage of its life cycle.
[0.000, 0.088, 0.054, 0.071, 0.484] Ori response: the sun is currently in the main sequence stage of its life cycle.

Prompt: when does april fools day end at noon
Ground truth: In Poland, prima aprilis ("1 April" in Latin) as a day of jokes is a centuries-long tradition. It is a day in which many jokes are told; various hoaxes--sometimes very sophisticated--are prepared by people, media (which often cooperate to make the "information" more credible) and even public institutions. Serious activities are usually avoided, and generally every word said on April 1st can be a lie, or a joke. The conviction for this is so strong that the Polish anti-Turkish alliance with Leopold I signed on April 1, 1683, was backdated to March 31. However, for some in Poland prima aprilis ends at noon of April 1st, and prima aprilis jokes after that hour are considered inappropriate and not classy.

It is a day where people play practical jokes and spread hoaxes on April 1st. The jokes and their victims are known as April Fools, and people playing these jokes often expose their prank with the phrase "April Fool!" The custom of setting aside a day for playing practical jokes and spreading false information is not a formal or official tradition, but rather a cultural phenomenon that is observed in some European and Western countries.

Prompt: how many times have the winter olympics been in the usa since 1924
Ground truth: The Winter Olympics has been hosted on three continents by twelve different countries. The Games have been held four times in the United States (in 1932, 1960, 1980 and 2002); three times in France (in 1924, 1968 and 1992); and twice each in Austria (1964, 1976), Canada (1988, 2010), Japan (1972, 1998), Italy (1956, 2006), Norway (1952, 1994), and Switzerland (1928, 1948). Also, the Games have been held just once each in Germany (1936), Yugoslavia (1984), Russia (2014) and South Korea (2018). The IOC has selected Beijing, China, to host the 2022 Winter Olympics and the host of the 2026 Winter Olympics will be selected in September 2019. As of 2018, no city in the southern hemisphere has applied to host the cold-weather-dependent Winter Olympics, which are held in February at the height of the southern hemisphere summer.

Prompt: the elements in each period have the same number of
Ground truth: A period in the periodic table is one of the horizontal rows, all of those elements have the same number of electron shells. Going across a period, each element has one more proton and is less metallic than its predecessor. Arranged this way, groups of elements in the same column have similar chemical and physical properties, reflecting the periodic law. For example, the alkali metals lie in the first column (group 1) and share similar properties, such as high reactivity and the tendency to lose one electron to arrive at a noble-gas electronic configuration. As of 2016 a total of 118 elements have been discovered and confirmed.

Prompt: who is recognized as the founder of islam
Ground truth: According to tradition, the Islamic prophet Muhammad was born in Mecca around the year 570. His family belonged to the Quraysh. When he was about forty years old, he began receiving what Muslims consider to be divine revelations delivered through the angel Gabriel, which would later form the Quran, enjoining him to proclaim a strict monotheistic faith, warn his compatriots of the impending Judgement Day, and castigate social injustices of his city. Muhammad's message won over a handful of followers and was met with increasing opposition from notables of Mecca. In 618, after he lost protection with the death of his influential uncle Abu Talib, Muhammad took flight to the city of Yathrib (subsequently called Medina) where he was joined by his followers. Later generations would count this event, known as the hijra, as the start of the Islamic era.

US 1 is generally paralleled by Interstate 95 (I-95), though the former is significantly farther west (inland) between Jacksonville, Florida, and Petersburg, Virginia. The highway connects most of the major cities of the East Coast--including Miami, Jacksonville, Richmond, Washington, D.C., Baltimore, Philadelphia, New York City and Boston, passing from the Southeastern United States to New England.

Prompt: where does the term dog and pony show come from
Ground truth: The term was originally used in the United States in the late-19th and early-20th centuries to refer to small traveling circuses that toured through small towns and rural areas. The name derives from the common use of performing dogs and ponies as the main attractions of the events. Performances were generally held in open-air arenas, such as race tracks or public spaces in localities that were too small or remote to attract larger, more elaborate performers or performances. The most notorious was "Prof. Gentry's Famous Dog & Pony Show," started when teenager Henry Gentry and his brothers started touring in 1886 with their act, originally entitled "Gentry's Equine and Canine Paradox." It started small, but evolved into a full circus show. Other early dog and pony shows included Morris' Equine and Canine Paradoxes (1883) and Hurlburt's Dog and Pony Show (late 1880s).

In Canada, parole is granted by the National Parole Board, which considers a variety of factors, including the prisoner's conduct while in prison, their rehabilitation efforts, and the risk they pose to society.

Ground truth: The 2016 UEFA Champions League Final was the final match of the 2015--16 UEFA Champions League, the 61st season of Europe's premier club football tournament organised by UEFA, and the 24th season since it was renamed from the European Champion Clubs' Cup to the UEFA Champions League. It was played at the San Siro stadium in Milan, Italy, on 28 May 2016, between Spanish teams Real Madrid and Atlético Madrid, in a repeat of the 2014 final. It was the second time in the tournament's history that both finalists were from the same city. Real Madrid won 5--3 on a penalty shoot-out after a 1--1 draw at the end of extra time, securing a record-extending 11th title in the competition.

Prompt: the origins of the stations of the cross
Ground truth: The Stations of the Cross or the Way of the Cross, also known as the Way of Sorrows or the Via Crucis, refers to a series of images depicting Jesus Christ on the day of his crucifixion and accompanying prayers. The stations grew out of imitations of Via Dolorosa in Jerusalem which is believed to be the actual path Jesus walked to Mount Calvary. The object of the stations is to help the Christians faithful to make a spiritual pilgrimage through contemplation of the Passion of Christ. It has become one of the most popular devotions and the stations can be found in many Western Christian churches, including Anglican, Lutheran, Methodist, and Roman Catholic ones.

Prompt: what does the sun represent on the uruguay flag
Ground truth: The horizontal stripes on the flag represent the nine original departments of Uruguay, based on the U.S flag, where the stripes represent the original 13 colonies. The first flag designed in 1828 had 9 light blue stripes; this number was reduced to 4 in 1830 due to visibility problems from distance. The Sun of May represents the May Revolution of 1810; according to the historian Diego Abad de Santillán, the Sun of May is a figurative sun that represents Inti, the sun god of the Inca religion. It also appears in the Flag of Argentina and the Coat of Arms of Bolivia.

Prompt: when did beryl markham fly across the atlantic
Ground truth: When Markham decided to take on the Atlantic crossing, no female pilot had yet flown non-stop from Europe to New York, and no woman had made the westward flight solo, though several had died trying. Markham hoped to claim both records. On 4 September 1936, she took off from Abingdon, England. After a 20-hour flight, her Vega Gull, The Messenger, suffered fuel starvation due to icing of the fuel tank vents, and she crash-landed at Baleine Cove on Cape Breton Island, Nova Scotia, Canada. She became the first person to make it from England to North America non-stop from east to west. She was celebrated as an aviation pioneer.

Prompt: when does a limit of a function not exist
Ground truth: Formal definitions, first devised in the early 19th century, are given below. Informally, a function f assigns an output f (x) to every input x. We say the function has a limit L at an input p: this means f (x) gets closer and closer to L as x moves closer and closer to p. More specifically, when f is applied to any input sufficiently close to p, the output value is forced arbitrarily close to L. On the other hand, if some inputs very close to p are taken to outputs that stay a fixed distance apart, we say the limit does not exist.
[0.253, 0.231, 0.069, 0.154, 0.514] Agent refined response: 

A limit of a function does not exist in the following cases:

1. As special cases, limits on an interval: A limit does not exist if the function is not defined on the entire interval or if the function is not continuous on the entire interval.
2. Left-hand limits of real-valued functions: A limit does not exist if s is an open interval of the form (−∞,a), where a is a real number.
3. Right-hand limits of real-valuED functions: A limit does not exist If s is an open interval of the forma (a,∞), where a is a real number
4. One-sided limits at included endpoints: A limit does not exist if x approaches the included endpoint of a half-closed interval from below.
[0.213, 0.268, 0.085, 0.148, 0.519] Ori response: 

A limit of a function does not exist in the following cases:

1. Special cases of limits on an interval: Limits do not exist for functions on certain intervals, such as left-hand limits of real-valued functions (e.g., by taking $s$ to be an open interval of the forms $(-\infty,a)$ or $(a,\infty)$) and right-hand limits (e.g., by taking$s$ to be an open interval such as $(a, \infty)$ or $(-\infty,a)$).
2. Included endpoints of closed intervals: The limit of a function does not exist as $x$ approaches $0$ from above when the interval is closed on the right side, but not on the left side. For example, the square root function $f(x) = \sqrt{x}$ has a limit of $0$ as $x$ approaches $0$, but only from the right side.
3. Deleted versus non-deleted limits: The concept of one-sided limits is extended to include the included endpoints of closed intervals. This means that the limit of a function may not exist if the interval is deleted, but it may exist

Prompt: where does eye of the round roast come from
Ground truth: A round steak is a beef steak from the "round", the rear leg of the cow. The round is divided into cuts including the eye (of) round, bottom round, and top round, with or without the "round" bone (femur), and may include the knuckle (sirloin tip), depending on how the round is separated from the loin. This is a lean cut and it is moderately tough. Lack of fat and marbling makes round dry out when cooked with dry-heat cooking methods like roasting or grilling. Round steak is commonly prepared with slow moist-heat methods including braising, to tenderize the meat and maintain moisture. The cut is often sliced thin, then dried or smoked at low temperature to make jerky.

Prompt: where do bullets go when fired in the air
Ground truth: Bullets fired into the air usually fall back with terminal velocities much lower than their muzzle velocity when they leave the barrel of a firearm. Nevertheless, people can be injured, sometimes fatally, when bullets discharged into the air fall back down to the ground. Bullets fired at angles less than vertical are more dangerous as the bullet maintains its angular ballistic trajectory and is far less likely to engage in tumbling motion; it therefore travels at speeds much higher than a bullet in free fall.
[0.753, 0.805, 0.611, 0.755, 0.888] Agent refined response: Bullets fired into the air usually fall with terminal velocities much lower than the muzzle velocity when they leave a firearm. Nevertheless, people can be injured or fatally when bullets discharged into air fall back down to the ground, despite the terminal velocity. [0.358, 0.456, 0.301, 0.377, 0.733] Ori response: Bullets fired into the air usually fall with terminal velocities much lower than the muzzle velocity when they leave a firearm's barrel. Nevertheless, people can be injured or even killed when bullets fired into the air fall back down to earth.

However, the terminal velocity of a bullet fired into the air depends on various factors, including the weight and size of the bullet, the air density, and the angle of the shot. Generally, the heavier and larger the bullet, the lower its terminal velocity.

It is important to note that even if the bullet falls back to the ground with a lower velocity than when it left the barrel, it can still cause significant damage or injury if it hits a person or object. Therefore, it is crucial to handle firearms safely and responsibly, especially when firing shots into the air.

Ground truth: The Triple Entente (from French entente (ɑ̃tɑ̃t) "friendship, understanding, agreement") refers to the understanding linking the Russian Empire, the French Third Republic, and the United Kingdom of Great Britain and Ireland after the signing of the Anglo-Russian Entente on 31 August 1907. Prompt: when was the national flag of india adopted
Ground truth: The National Flag of India is a horizontal rectangular tricolour of India saffron, white and India green; with the Ashoka Chakra, a 24-spoke wheel, in navy blue at its centre. It was adopted in its present form during a meeting of the Constituent Assembly held on 22 July 1947, and it became the official flag of the Dominion of India on 15 August 1947. The flag was subsequently retained as that of the Republic of India. In India, the term "tricolour" (Hindi: तिरंगा, translit. Tiraṅgā) almost always refers to the Indian national flag. The flag is based on the Swaraj flag, a flag of the Indian National Congress designed by Pingali Venkayya.
[0.000, 0.052, 0.035, 0.052, 0.325] Agent refined response: 15 August 1947
[0.000, 0.052, 0.035, 0.052, 0.302] Ori response: 15 August 1947.

Prompt: when does canada switch to daylight savings time
Ground truth: In regions where daylight saving time is used, it commences on the second Sunday of March, and standard time restarts on the first Sunday in November.
[0.079, 0.196, 0.069, 0.137, 0.545] Agent refined response: Canada observes Daylight Saving Time (DST) in all ten Canadian provinces and three territories. However, there are exceptions within several provinces, including most of Saskatchewan, which observers Central Standard Time year-round, even though the province is in the Mountain zone, effectively putting it on DST year-round.

In Canada, the start and end dates of DST vary by province or territory. Here are the approximate start and end dates of DST in each province or territory:

* British Columbia: Second Sunday in March (around March  14) to first Sunday in November (around November 7)
* Nunavut: Last Sunday in March (around March  28) to last Sunday in October (around October 31)
* Ontario: First Sunday in March (around March 7) to last Sunday in October ( around October 31)
* Quebec: Second Sunday in March (around march 14) to last Sunday in October (approximately October 31)
* Saskatchewan: Central Standard Time year-round, except for a brief period in the summer when DST is observed.

It is important to note that these dates are approximate and may vary slightly from year to year
[0.234, 0.447, 0.261, 0.362, 0.655] Ori response: 

Canada observes Daylight Saving Time (DST) in all ten Canadian provinces and three territories. However, there are exceptions within several provinces, including most of Saskatchewan, which observers Central Standard Time year-round, even though the province is in the Mountain zone, effectively putting it on DST year-round. Under the Canadian law, DST begins on the second Sunday in March and ends on the first Sunday in November.

Prompt: who is often associated with printing the first book using moveable type in germany
Ground truth: Johannes Gutenberg of Mainz, Germany is acknowledged as the first to invent a metal movable-type printing system in Europe, the printing press. Gutenberg was a goldsmith familiar with techniques of cutting punches for making coins from moulds. Between 1436 and 1450 he developed hardware and techniques for casting letters from matrices using a device called the hand mould. Gutenberg's key invention and contribution to movable-type printing in Europe, the hand mould, was the first practical means of making cheap copies of letterpunches in the vast quantities needed to print complete books, making the movable-type printing process a viable enterprise.

Prompt: where does the saying keeping up with the jones come from
Ground truth: The phrase originates with the comic strip Keeping Up with the Joneses, created by Arthur R. "Pop" Momand in 1913. The strip ran until 1940 in The New York World and various other newspapers. The strip depicts the social climbing McGinis family, who struggle to "keep up" with their neighbors, the Joneses of the title. The Joneses were unseen characters throughout the strip's run, often spoken of but never shown. The idiom keeping up with the Joneses has remained popular long after the strip's end.
[0.358, 0.611, 0.527, 0.534, 0.771] Agent refined response: 

The phrase "Keeping up with the Joneses" originates from the comic strip "Keeping Up with the Joneses" created by Arthur R. "Pop" Momand in 1913, which depicted the social climbing McGinis family struggling to keep up with their neighbors, the Joneses of the title.
[0.600, 0.581, 0.412, 0.477, 0.710] Ori response: 

The phrase "Keeping up with the Joneses" originates from the comic strip "Keeping Up with the Joneses" created by Arthur R. "Pop" Momand in 1913, which ran until 1940. The strip depicts the social climbers, the McGuinis, who struggle to keep up with their neighbors, the Joneses, in terms of social status and material possessions. The phrase became a common idiom used to describe the feeling of inferiority or inadequacy when comparing oneself to others, particularly when it comes to socio-economic or cultural status.

Prompt: what role does the president play in foreign affairs
Ground truth: Subject to the advice and consent role of the U.S. Senate, the President of the United States negotiates treaties with foreign nations, but treaties enter into force if ratified by two-thirds of the Senate. The President is also Commander in Chief of the United States Armed Forces, and as such has broad authority over the armed forces. Both the Secretary of State and ambassadors are appointed by the President, with the advice and consent of the Senate. The United States Secretary of State acts similarly to a foreign minister and under Executive leadership is the primary conductor of state-to-state diplomacy.
[0.583, 0.595, 0.291, 0.307, 0.703] Agent refined response: 

The president plays a crucial role in foreign affairs, with the advice and consent of Congress. The President acts as the primary conductor of state-to-state diplomacy, and the United States Secretary of State acts similarly to a foreign minister. The President has the power to negotiate and sign treaties, and the Senate must ratify them. The President also has the authority to declare war, with the War Powers Clause of the Constitution giving him the power to do so in the absence of a declaration of war by Congress. Additionally, the President has the authority to appoint ambassadors and other diplomatic officials, with the advice and consent of Senate.
[0.569, 0.638, 0.350, 0.346, 0.729] Ori response: 

The president plays a crucial role in foreign affairs as the President of the United States, with the advice and consent of Congress. The President is the primary conductor of state-to-state diplomacy, and the United States Secretary of State acts similarly to a foreign minister. The President has the power to negotiate and ratify treaties, appoint ambassadors, and recognize foreign governments. The President also has the authority to deploy the military and declare war with the approval of Congress.

Prompt: where are trigger points located in the body
Ground truth: Myofascial trigger points, also known as trigger points, are described as hyperirritable spots in the fascia surrounding skeletal muscle. They are associated with palpable nodules in taut bands of muscle fibers. They are a topic of ongoing controversy, as there is limited data to inform a scientific understanding of the phenomenon. Accordingly, a formal acceptance of myofascial "knots" as an identifiable source of pain is more common among bodyworkers, physical therapists, chiropractors, and osteopathic practitioners. Nonetheless, the concept of trigger points provides a framework which may be used to help address certain musculoskeletal pain.

Prompt: what is foreign account tax compliance act (fatca)
Ground truth: The Foreign Account Tax Compliance Act (FATCA) is a 2010 United States federal law requiring all non-U.S. (' foreign ') financial institutions (FFIs) to search their records for customers with indicia of ' U.S.-person ' status, such as a U.S. place of birth, and to report the assets and identities of such persons to the U.S. Department of the Treasury. FATCA also requires such persons to self-report their non-U.S. financial assets annually to the Internal Revenue Service (IRS) on form 8938, which is in addition to the older and further redundant requirement to self-report them annually to the Financial Crimes Enforcement Network (FinCEN) on form 114 (also known as' FBAR '). Like U.S. income tax law, FATCA applies to U.S. residents and also to U.S. citizens and green card holders residing in other countries.
[0.579, 0.755, 0.695, 0.739, 0.889] Agent refined response: Foreign Account Tax Compliance Act (FATCA) is a 2010 United States federal law that requires all non-U.S. ("foreign") financial institutions (FFIs) to search their records for customers with "indicia of U.S. person status," such as a U.S. place of birth, and to reported the assets and identities of such person to the U.S. Department of the Treasury. FATCA also requires such persons to self-report their non-U.S. financial assets annually to the Internal Revenue Service (IRS) on Form 8938, which are in addition to the older FBAR (Foreign Bank Account Report) requirement.
[0.636, 0.805, 0.754, 0.789, 0.888] Ori response: 

The Foreign Account Tax Compliance Act (FATCA) is a 2010 United States federal law requiring all non-U.S. ("foreign") financial institutions (FFIs) to search their records for customers with indicator of U.S. person status, such as a U.S. place of birth, and to  report the assets and identities of  such persons to the U.S. Department of the Treasury. The pars distalis contains two types of cells including chromophobe cells and chromophil cells. The chromophils can be further divided into acidophils (alpha cells) and basophils (beta cells). These cells all together produce hormones of the anterior pituitary, and release them into the blood stream.
[0.330, 0.329, 0.093, 0.211, 0.532] Agent refined response: 

The hormones of the anterior pitutary gland are created through the following process:

1. Stress: Stress induces the release of corticotropin-releasing hormone (CRH) and vasopressin from the hypalamus, which activates te release of adrenocorticotrophic hormone (ACTH) from the anterior pituitary Gland.
2. ACTH release: ACTH is released from the anterior pituitary and acts on the adrenal cortexto produce glucocorticoids, such as cortisol.
3. Glucocorticoids action: Glucocorticoids act back ont the anterior pituitary gand the hypothalamus with negative feedack to slow the production of CRH.
[0.348, 0.326, 0.101, 0.227, 0.530] Ori response: 

The hormones of the anterior psuedopal gland are created in the following places:

1. Corticotropin-releasing hormone (CRH): Hypothalamus
2. Vasopressin: Hypothalamus
3. Adrenocorticotropic hitterone (ACTH): Hypothalamus.

Stress activates the release of CRH and vasopressin from the Hypothalamus, which activates ACTH from the anterior pituitary, leading to the production of glucocorticoids such a cortisol. These glucocorticoids act on the anterior pituitary and the hypothalamus with the negative feedback to slow the production of CRH.

Prompt: communities of similar organisms found in a particular environment are called
Ground truth: In ecology, a habitat is the kind of natural environment in which a particular species of organism lives. It is characterized by both physical and biological features. A species' habitat is those places where it can find food, shelter, protection and mates for reproduction.
[0.000, 0.082, 0.000, 0.082, 0.392] Agent refined response: 

community of plants and animals.
[0.138, 0.203, 0.011, 0.139, 0.570] Ori response: 

Ecosystems, biomes, and communities are all terms used to describe particular types of communities of living organisms found in a particular environment.

* An ecosystem is a community of living and non-living things in a particular environment, including plants, animals, microorganisms, and physical factors such as soil, water, and air.
* A biome is a large community of plants and animals that have similar environmental conditions and are found in a particular geographical area.
* A community is a group of living organisms of the same or related species that live in the same environment and interact with one another.

For example, a coral reef community is a group of plants and animals that live in a warm, shallow ocean environment with high levels of sunlight, nutrients, and water clarity. The community may include coral polyps, fish, sea turtles, sea urchins, and many other species.

Prompt: what is the full scientific name for the e. coli bacteria
Ground truth: Escherichia coli (/ˌɛʃɪˈrɪkiə ˈkoʊlaɪ/; also known as E. coli) is a Gram-negative, facultatively anaerobic, rod-shaped, coliform bacterium of the genus Escherichia that is commonly found in the lower intestine of warm-blooded organisms (endotherms). Most E. coli strains are harmless, but some serotypes can cause serious food poisoning in their hosts, and are occasionally responsible for product recalls due to food contamination. The harmless strains are part of the normal flora of the gut, and can benefit their hosts by producing vitamin K, and preventing colonization of the intestine with pathogenic bacteria, having a symbiotic relationship. E. coli is expelled into the environment within fecal matter. The bacterium grows massively in fresh fecal matter under aerobic conditions for 3 days, but its numbers decline slowly afterwards.
[0.000, 0.127, 0.043, 0.099, 0.492] Agent refined response: 

The full scientific name for Escherichia coli (E. coli) is Escherichia coli.
[0.002, 0.151, 0.056, 0.096, 0.556] Ori response: 

The full scientific name for Escherichia coli (E. coli) is Escherichia coli (Gram-negative, facultative anaerobe).

Prompt: how long did it take to build the great pyramid of egypt
Ground truth: Egyptologists believe the pyramid was built as a tomb for the Fourth Dynasty Egyptian pharaoh Khufu (often Hellenized as "Cheops") and was constructed over a 20-year period. Khufu's vizier, Hemiunu (also called Hemon) is believed by some to be the architect of the Great Pyramid. It is thought that, at construction, the Great Pyramid was originally 280 Egyptian Royal cubits tall (146.5 metres (480.6 ft)), but with erosion and absence of its pyramidion, its present height is 138.8 metres (455.4 ft). Each base side was 440 cubits, 230.4 metres (755.9 ft) long. The mass of the pyramid is estimated at 5.9 million tonnes. The volume, including an internal hillock, is roughly 2,500,000 cubic metres (88,000,000 cu ft).
[0.112, 0.253, 0.089, 0.165, 0.528] Agent refined response: The Great Pyramid of Giza was built over a 14-year period, with a peak workforce of roughly 30,000 workers. Without the use of pulleys, wheel, or iron tools, they used "critical path analysis methods," which suggest that the Great Pyramid was completed from start to finished in approximately  10 years.
[0.214, 0.295, 0.074, 0.166, 0.533] Ori response: The Great Pyramid of Giza was built over a 14-year period, with a peak workforce of around 40,000 workers and an average workforce of about 20,000 workers. This estimate is based on a modern construction management study in association with Mark Lehner and other Egyptologists.

Without the use of pulleys, winches, or iron tools, the ancient Egyptians used critical path analysis methods to construct the Great Pyramid. According to these methods, the Great Pyramid was completed from start to completion in approximately 10 years.

Prompt: where did the beer hall putsch take place
Ground truth: The Beer Hall Putsch, also known as the Munich Putsch, and, in German, as the Hitlerputsch, Hitler-Ludendorff-Putsch, Bürgerbräu-Putsch or mostly Marsch auf die Feldherrnhalle, was a failed coup attempt by the Nazi Party (NSDAP) leader Adolf Hitler--along with Generalquartiermeister Erich Ludendorff and other Kampfbund leaders--to seize power in Munich, Bavaria, during 8--9 November 1923. About two thousand Nazis marched to the centre of Munich, where they confronted the police, which resulted in the death of 16 Nazis and four police officers. Hitler was not wounded during the clash, although he locked his left arm with the right arm of Max Erwin von Scheubner-Richter who, when he was shot and killed, pulled Hitler to the pavement with him. Hitler escaped immediate arrest and was spirited off to safety in the countryside. After two days, Hitler was arrested and charged with treason.

Prompt: who said beware of the ides of march
Ground truth: In modern times, the Ides of March is best known as the date on which Julius Caesar was assassinated in 44 BC. Caesar was stabbed to death at a meeting of the Senate. As many as 60 conspirators, led by Brutus and Cassius, were involved. According to Plutarch, a seer had warned that harm would come to Caesar no later than the Ides of March. On his way to the Theatre of Pompey, where he would be assassinated, Caesar passed the seer and joked, "The Ides of March are come", implying that the prophecy had not been fulfilled, to which the seer replied "Aye, Caesar; but not gone." This meeting is famously dramatised in William Shakespeare's play Julius Caesar, when Caesar is warned by the soothsayer to "beware the Ides of March." The Roman biographer Suetonius identifies the "seer" as a haruspex named Spurinna.

Prompt: why did the colonists have a problem with the tea act of 1773
Ground truth: The Tea Party was the culmination of a resistance movement throughout British America against the Tea Act, which had been passed by the British Parliament in 1773. Colonists objected to the Tea Act because they believed that it violated their rights as Englishmen to "No taxation without representation", that is, to be taxed only by their own elected representatives and not by a British parliament in which they were not represented. In addition, the well-connected East India Company had been granted competitive advantages over colonial tea importers, who resented the move and feared additional infringement on their business. Protesters had successfully prevented the unloading of taxed tea in three other colonies, but in Boston, embattled Royal Governor Thomas Hutchinson refused to allow the tea to be returned to Britain.

Ground truth: Claims adjuster (claim adjuster), or claims handler (claim handler), investigates insurance claims by interviewing the claimant and witnesses, consulting police and hospital records, and inspecting property damage to determine the extent of the company's liability. In the United Kingdom, Ireland, Australia, South Africa, the Caribbean and New Zealand the term loss adjuster is used. Other claims adjusters who represent policyholders may aid in the preparation of an insurance claim.

A claims adjuster or public adjuster represents the insured in the investigation and settlement of a claim. They do not engage in the practice of law and their role is to evaluate the covered injuries or damages determined according to the coverage grants, negotiate a settlement according to the law, and identify coverages for which the Insured is covered, following best insurances practices.

Prompt: when does a dieback or population crash occur
Ground truth: In population dynamics and population ecology, overshoot occurs when a population temporarily exceeds the long term carrying capacity of its environment. The environment usually has mechanisms in place to prevent overshoot. For example, plants are only able to regenerate and regrow a few times after being consumed before completely dying off. The consequence of overshoot is called a collapse, a crash or a die-off in which there is a decline in population density. The entire sequence or trajectory undergone by the population and its environment together is often termed ' overshoot-and-collapse '.
[0.134, 0.338, 0.109, 0.231, 0.597] Agent refined response: 

A dieback or population crash occurs when the rate of reproduction is higher than the death rate, leading to an increase in population density, which can cause overshoot and ultimately result in a decline in population density.
[0.327, 0.329, 0.107, 0.212, 0.608] Ori response: 

A dieback or population crash occurs when a population experiences a decline in population density due to overshoot. This can happen when reproduction rates remain high relative to the death rate, leading to an increase in population size. However, if the population grows too quickly, it can lead to a decline in population density due a shortage of resources, such as food, water, or habitat. This decline in population density can result in a dieback or crash.

Prompt: what states do not allow daylight savings time
Ground truth: Daylight saving time in the United States is the practice of setting the clock forward by one hour during the warmer part of the year, so that evenings have more daylight and mornings have less. Most areas of the United States observe daylight saving time (DST), the exceptions being Arizona (except for the Navajo, who do observe daylight saving time on tribal lands), Hawaii, and the overseas territories of American Samoa, Guam, the Northern Mariana Islands, Puerto Rico, and the United States Virgin Islands. The Uniform Time Act of 1966 established the system of uniform Daylight Saving Time throughout the US.
[0.067, 0.369, 0.266, 0.308, 0.649] Agent refined response:

Prompt: who explored waters of cuba the bahamas and hispaniola
Ground truth: In 1492 Christopher Columbus sailed from Spain on his first voyage with three ships, the Niña, the Pinta, and the flagship, Santa Maria, seeking a direct route to Asia. On 12 October 1492 Columbus reached an island in the Bahamas and claimed it for Spain, an event long regarded by Europeans as the ' discovery ' of America. This island was called Guanahani by the Lucayan, and San Salvador by the Spanish. The identity of the first American landfall by Columbus remains controversial, but many authors accept Samuel E. Morison's identification of Columbus' San Salvador as what was later called Watling (or Watling's) Island. Its name has been officially changed to San Salvador. Prompt: where is connective tissue found in the body
Ground truth: Connective tissue (CT) is one of the four basic types of animal tissue, along with epithelial tissue, muscle tissue, and nervous tissue. It develops from the mesoderm. Connective tissue is found in between other tissues everywhere in the body, including the nervous system. In the central nervous system, the three outer membranes (the meninges) that envelop the brain and spinal cord are composed of connective tissue. They support and protect the body. All connective tissue consists of three main components: fibers (elastic and collagenous fibers), ground substance and cells. Not all authorities include blood or lymph as connective tissue because they lack the fiber component. All are immersed in the body water.

In other parts of the body, connective tissue is found in the following places:

1. Blood vessels: Connective tissue wraps around blood vessels to keep them in place and to secure them to surrounding tissues.
2. Lymphatic system: The lymphatic system, which helps the body eliminate waste and excess fluids, is supported by connective tissue.
3. Joints: Cartilage, a type of connective tissue, is found in joints and helps to absorb shock and keep bones in place.
4. Tendons: Tendons, which connect muscles to bones, are made of connective tissue.
5. Eye: The cornea, iris, and retina are all made of connective tissue in the eye.
6. Skin: Connective tissue underlies the skin and helps to hold it in place.
7. Heart: The heart muscle is made of connective t

Prompt: where are the cones in the eye located
Ground truth: Cone cells, or cones, are one of three types of photoreceptor cells in the retina of mammalian eyes (e.g. the human eye). They are responsible for color vision and function best in relatively bright light, as opposed to rod cells, which work better in dim light. Cone cells are densely packed in the fovea centralis, a 0.3 mm diameter rod-free area with very thin, densely packed cones which quickly reduce in number towards the periphery of the retina. There are about six to seven million cones in a human eye and are most concentrated towards the macula. The commonly cited figure of six million cone cells in the human eye was found by Osterberg in 1935. Oyster's textbook (1999) cites work by Curcio et al. (1990) indicating an average close to 4.5 million cone cells and 90 million rod cells in the human retina.
[0.019, 0.219, 0.099, 0.186, 0.588] Agent refined response: 

Cones are located in the fovea, which is the central part of the retina, and are much less numerous than rod cells in most parts of the retina but greatly outnumber rods in fovea.
[0.006, 0.169, 0.068, 0.157, 0.546] Ori response: 

Cones are located in the fovea and are much less numerous than roods in most parts of the retina but greatly outnumber rods in most parts of the fovea.

Prompt: where do you get male pattern baldness from
Ground truth: Male pattern hair loss is believed to be due to a combination of genetics and the male hormone dihydrotestosterone. The cause in female pattern hair loss remains unclear.
[0.148, 0.263, 0.114, 0.200, 0.605] Agent refined response: Male pattern baldness, also known as androgenetic alopecia, is a common condition in which men experience hair loss due to the presence of the male hormone dihydrotestosterone (DHT) in their bodies. DHT is a potent form of testosterone that is produced by the enzyme 5-alpha-reductase in the hair follicles.

As men age, the levels of DHT in their bodies increase, leading to a gradual shrinking of the hair follicles, resulting in hair loss. This condition is inherited, and the risk of developing male pattern baldness increases with age.

Other factors, such as family history, genetics, stress, and certain medical conditions, can also contribute to hair loss. Marital status has been shown in some cross-sectional studies to influence hair loss, with married men experiencing less hair loss than unmarried men.
[0.170, 0.289, 0.160, 0.224, 0.661] Ori response: Male pattern baldness, also known as androgenetic alopecia, is a common condition in which men experience hair loss due to a combination of genetic and hormonal factors. It is caused by the gradual reduction of hair follicles in the frontal and vertex areas of the scalp, leading to thinning and eventual baldness.

While the exact causes of male pattern baldness are not fully understood, it is believed to be linked to the presence of the male hormone dihydrotestosterone (DHT) in the body. DHT is a potent form of testosterone that is produced by the enzyme 5-alpha-reductase in the hair follicles. As men age, the amount of DHT in their bodies increases, leading to a gradual reduction in hair growth and eventual baldness.

Prompt: the elements in each period have the same number of
Ground truth: A period in the periodic table is one of the horizontal rows, all of those elements have the same number of electron shells. Going across a period, each element has one more proton and is less metallic than its predecessor. Arranged this way, groups of elements in the same column have similar chemical and physical properties, reflecting the periodic law. For example, the alkali metals lie in the first column (group 1) and share similar properties, such as high reactivity and the tendency to lose one electron to arrive at a noble-gas electronic configuration. As of 2016 a total of 118 elements have been discovered and confirmed.

Prompt: where do the secretory cells of endocrine glands secrete their products
Ground truth: Exocrine glands are glands that produce and secrete substances onto an epithelial surface by way of a duct. Examples of exocrine glands include sweat, salivary, mammary, ceruminous, lacrimal, sebaceous, and mucous. Exocrine glands are one of two types of glands in the human body, the other being endocrine glands, which secrete their products directly into the bloodstream. The liver and pancreas are both exocrine and endocrine glands; they are exocrine glands because they secrete products--bile and pancreatic juice--into the gastrointestinal tract through a series of ducts, and endocrine because they secrete other substances directly into the bloodstream.
[0.244, 0.298, 0.013, 0.174, 0.591] Agent refined response: 

Secretory cells of endocrine gland excrete their products through the following mechanisms:

1. Serous cells secrete proteins, including enzymes. Examples include gastric chief cells and Paneth cells.
2. Mucous cells secrete mucin. Examples include Brunner's glands, esphageal glands, and plyoric glands.

3. Mixed glands secrete both proteins and mucin. Examples include the salivary glands, although the parotid gland is predominantly serous.
